Laminaria Pilot South1 Well Completion Report ( Basic Data )

1 INTRODUCTION

Laminaria Pilot South1 was drilled as a vertical appraisal well designed to verify the
structural uncertainty and sweep efficiency within the Laminaria reservoir . The well was
drilled by the semisubmersible drilling unit Atwood Eagle in Production Licence ACL5
within the Bonaparte Basin some 550 km west northwest of Darwin ( Figure 1 ) . The
Laminaria Pilot South1 well is located 940 metres north and 1250 metres south of the
Laminaria3ST1 and Laminaria6 surface locations respectively . Water depth at the
Laminaria Pilot South1 location was 352.2 metres at lowest astronomical tide ( LAT ) and
the rotary table elevation was 22.3 metres . Depth measurements in this report are with
reference to the rotary table and indicated by MRT .

The Atwood Eagle arrived on location on 23 May 2005 and Laminaria Pilot South1 was
spudded the next day . The total depth of 3338 mRT was reached on 05 June 2005 . The well
was plugged and abandoned and the Atwood Eagle released from contract on 09 June 2005
after a total of 16.96 days on the well . The estimated final well cost was A59.18 million .

Laminaria Pilot South1 Well Completion Report ( Basic Data )

2 OPERATIONS SUMMARY

Laminaria Pilot South1 was drilled by the semisubmersible drilling unit Atwood Eagle in
Production Licence ACL5 . The Atwood Eagle moved from the Laminaria5 intervention to
the Laminaria Pilot South1 location at 07:00hrs on 23 May 2005 . While setting anchors and
ballasting down the 914mm ( 36 ) Bottom Hole Assembly ( BHA ) was made up to the
Temporary Guide Base ( TGB ) in the moonpool and run to seabed .

Laminaria Pilot South1 was spudded at 03:15hrs on 24 May 2005 . The 914mm hole was
drilled to a depth of 410 mRT with seawater and sweeps . The 762x340mm ( 30x13.375 )
conductor ( with HAC connection ) was run with the Permanent Guide Base ( PGB ) to 407.3
MRT and cemented to surface .

The 311mm ( 12.25 ) hole was drilled riserless with seawater and hivis sweeps to a depth of
2694 MRT . The wellhead was run and successfully landed : the 244mm ( 9.625 ) casing was
run and casing was cemented with the shoe at 2688.8 mRT . The BOP stack and riser was
run and tested .

While making up a dog collar to the 171.5mm ( 6.75 ) RLL ( Formation Evaluation While
Drilling ) tool for the 216Mm ( 8.5 ) BHA the rectangular washer slid off the bolt and into the
hole . After unsuccessfully fishing with a fishing magnet assembly the fish was finally
recovered with a reverse circulating junk basket .

The casing float shoe and a 3 metre rathole were drilled prior to performing a Formation
Interval Test ( FIT ) test to 1.35 sg Equivalent Mudweight ( EMW ) . The 216mm hole was then
drilled to 2763 mRT at which point the mud motor failed and the bit became plugged with
motor rubber . The BHA was pulled out of the hole and the bit and motor replaced . The
216mm hole was then drilled to the Total Depth ( TD ) of 3338MRT .

The well was abandoned with three cement plugs prior to cutting the 244mm casing and
recovering the wellhead permanent and temporary guide bases and 762mm conductor back
to surface . The rig was deballasted the anchors pulled and the rig departed the Laminaria
Pilot South1 location at 06:00hrs on 09 June 2005 . Total well duration for Laminaria Pilot
South1 was 16.96 days and the estimated final cost is A59.18MM .

The Daily Drilling Reports Casing and Cementing Summaries Bit Record and Mud
Properties Table are contained in Appendices 1 to 4 .

3

Laminaria Pilot South1 Well Completion Report ( Basic Data )

3 FORMATION SAMPLING

A total of 1500g of ditch cuttings was collected at each sample point at 3 to 10 metre
intervals from 2694 to 3338 mRT in Laminaria Pilot South1 . The washed and airdried
samples were split into five sets ( Sets 1 to 5 ) of approximately 200 g samples and one set
( Set 6 ) of 30 g samples and placed in ziplock bags . One set of cuttings samples was
collected in samplex trays .

Set 1 was despatched to Geoscience Australia co Australian Geological Survey
Organisation ( AGSO ) Symonston ACT and Set 2 to the NTGS Core Library Winnellie NT .

The remaining sets were retained by Woodside and are located at Core Laboratories
Australia Pty . Ltd. 44 Belmont Avenue Kewdale WA .

3.1 Sidewall Cores

No sidewall cores were taken in Laminaria Pilot South1 .

3.2 Conventional Cores

No coring was conducted in Laminaria Pilot South1 .

3.3 Mud Gas Samples

Twentysix Mud Gas Isotope Logging ( MGIL ) samples were collected from 2750 to 3338 mRT
in Laminaria Pilot South1 and are held at Core Laboratories Australia Pty Ltd Kewdale WA .

4 FORMATION EVALUATION
41 Mudlogging

Baker Hughes Inteq provided mudlogging services for the drilling of Laminaria Pilot South1 .
This included conventional mudlogging formation evaluation real time data monitoring
pressure and drilling analyses . Baker Hughes End of Well Report and Formation Evaluation
Log Drilling Plot Gas Ratio Plot and Pressure Evaluation plot are contained in Appendix 7 .
The digital mudlogging data for Laminaria Pilot South1 are also attached to Appendix 7 .

42 Lithological Logging
Lithology and hydrocarbon shows are described in the Daily Geological Reports ( Appendix

5 ) . Cuttings were described by the wellsite geologists from 2694 to 3338 mRT in Laminaria
Pilot South1 and recorded on the Wellsite Lithology Log ( Appendix 6 ) .

4.3 Hydrocarbon Indications

Chromatographic breakdown of the ditch gas total gas and trip gas was recorded from 2694
to 3338 MRT ( Appendix 7 ) .

44 Measurements While Drilling ( MWD )

SperrySun Drilling Services provided Measurements While Drilling ( MWD ) and directional
drilling services in Laminaria Pilot South1 .

SperrySun recorded directional and drilling data throughout . Gamma ray was recorded in
the 311mm and 216mm hole sections . Resistivity neutron porosity and bulk density were
also recorded in the 216mm hole . All realtime and recorded data were recovered .

Full details of the MWD and directional drilling operations are contained in SperrySuns End
of Well Report ( Appendix 8 ) .

4.5 Wireline Logging

No wireline logging was performed in Laminaria Pilot South1 .

4.6 Velocity Survey

No velocity survey was performed in Laminaria Pilot South1 .

4.7 . Biostratigraphy

No biostratigraphic analyses were performed on samples from Laminaria Pilot South1 .

4.8 Geochemistry

No geochemical analyses were performed on cuttings samples from Laminaria Pilot South1 .

49 Petrology

No petrological analyses were performed on cuttings samples from Laminaria Pilot South1 .

Ops 00:00 to 06:00 : Continued to drill 311 mm ( 1214 ) hole riserless with seawater and hivis sweeps from 464.0m 923.0m .

Ops Summary ( 24 Hrs ) : Tagged seabed and landed TGB . Drilled 914mm ( 36 ) hole from 374.5m 410.0m and POOH . Ran and
cemented 3 joint 762 mm ( 30 ) conductor . Picked up 311mm ( 1214 ) BHA and RIH . Tagged shoe at 407.3m and commenced
drilling 311mm ( 1214 ) hole to 464.0m .

Ops Lookahead : Drill 311 mm ( 1214 ) hole riserless with seawater and hivis sweeps .

Operation

Continued to RIH with 914 mm ( 36 ) BHA and drill ahead TGB to 336.0m ( 1 stand
above seabed ) while ballasting rig to drilling draft .

Performed seabed survey with ROV seabed flat observed 1 minor object on sonar
40m away from well . Unable to perform survey off critical path due to backloading of
completion equipment onto Far Saltire on port side .

Rotated drillstring 30 deg to the left to orientate TGB . Continued to RIH and landed
TGB . TGB heading 088 deg ( rig heading 091 deg ) inclination O deg . Disengaged
drillahead dogs with ROV and tagged seabed with 914 mm ( 36 ) bit at 374.5m RT
( LAT ) 352.2m ( LAT ) water depth 22.3m air gap .

Spudded Laminaria Pilot South1 at 03:15 hrs 240505 . Drilled 36 hole from 374.5m
410.0m . WOB : 0.9t ( 2 klbs ) torque : 2.7 4.1 ( 23 kftlbs ) 3080 rpm flowrate :
3.8m3min ( 1000 gpm ) SPP : 8.3MPa ( 1200 psi ) . Average ROP : 47mhr .

Swept hole with 23.8 m3 ( 150bbl ) gel and displaced hole to 39.7 m3 ( 250 bbl ) gel mud
while reciprocating the drillstring .

POOH from 410.0 374.5m . Good hole condition no overpulls observed . Continued to

derrick .

Cleared rig floor . Held JSA prior to rigginig up to run 211mm ( 958 ) casing . Changed

Ops 00:00 to 06:00 : Landed 476 mm ( 1834 ) wellhead in 762 mm ( 30 ) housing . Cemented 244 mm ( 958 ) casing unlatched
running tool and commenced POOH .

Ops Summary ( 24 Hrs ) : Ran shoetrack and 186 joints of 244mm ( 958 ) casing . Made up 476mm ( 1834 ) wellhead to casing
string and commenced RIH on landing string .

Ops Lookahead : Lay out 241mm ( 912 ) FEWD and motor . Commence running BOP on marine riser .

Operation

Held JSA . Completed rig up of 244mm ( 958 ) casing equipment : landed FMS in
rotary picked up 350t slip type elevators and spotted TAM control unit on rig floor .

Held JSA . Picked up and checked flow through the shoe joint . Made up and
bakerlocked intermediate joint .

Performed troubleshooting on FMS safety switch . This switch ensures FMS and
elevators can not be open at the same time . Drillers display indicated FMS was open
even when FMS was closed . This was caused by misalignment of the safety switch with
the levelling beam . Realigned bracket supporting safety switch . Tested OK .

Picked up bakerlocked and checked flow through float collar joint . Picked up and ran
28 joints of 244mm ( 958 ) casing to 370m ( above seabed ) . Installed centralisers on
the first 5 joints . Filled every joint with seawater through the TAM packer .

Due to strong currents ROV observed casing shoe 12m on a bearing of 070 deg from
PGB . Kedged rig to conductor location . Large mound of cuttings on the forward side of
the PGB . Staged up pumps to 3.8 m3min ( 1000 gpm ) and jetted PGB for 10 minutes .
Subsea currents eased significantly . PGB location from the drillstring 10m at a
bearing of 330 degrees . Kedged rig over location . Held casing shoe with ROV arm and
stabbed into 762mm ( 30 ) conductor .

Picked up and ran remaining 158 joints of 244mm ( 958 ) casing to 2305.9m @ 14
jntshr . Pick up weight : 205.3t ( 460 klbs ) slack off weight:187.5t ( 420 kibs ) . Filled every
joint with seawater through the TAM packer . Average casing running speed for the past
24hrs : 13.5 jointshr .

Held JSA prior to rigging down casing handling equipment . Swapped out bails broke
out TAM packer swapped out elevators and removed FMS . Left TAM packer hydraulic
line in the derrick for Pelatonia .

Picked up 476mm ( 1834 ) wellhead . Rotated casing string to ensure antirotation fin
on 508mm ( 20 ) joint does not collide with HAC conduit on 762mm ( 30 ) conductor .
Commenced running 244mm ( 958 ) casing on 140mm ( 512 ) drillpipe drifted each
stand . At 2611m broke circulation at 0.27 m3min ( 72 gpm ) with 2.1MPa ( 300 psi ) and
commenced washing down to 2479.3m . Pickup weight of string : 212t ( 475klbs ) slackoff
weight : 194.2 ( 435 kibs ) .

( 27 bbls ) driliwater at 0.6 m3min ( 4 bblmin ) observed top plug launch .

displacing pumping at 0.9m3min ( 250gpm ) . Increased pumps t013.7 m3min ( 600
9pm ) . Observed bottom plug shear at 1.9MPa ( 280 psi ) 3.0m3 ( 19 bbl ) early .
Continued displacing at 1.4m3min ( 8.5 bblmin ) . Slowed pumps to 0.6 m3min ( 4
bblmin ) 4.8m3 ( 30 bbl ) prior to theoretical bump strokes . Observed bottom plug bump
3.7m3 ( 23.3bbl ) early ( assuming 97Y6 pump efficiency ) . Bumped plug with 6.8 MPa
( 980 psi ) ( 3.4MPa 500 psi over initial bump pressure ) . Switched to cement unit .
Pressure tested casing to 24.1 MPa ( 3500 psi ) for 10 min tested OK pumped 2.3 m3
( 5 bbl ) . Bled back 2.3 m3 ( 8 bbl ) 0.9m3 ( 3 bbl ) line volume . Floats held . Good returns
observed by ROV throughout the cement job . Estimate TOC 268m above casing
shoe from pressure differential observed . Cement in place at 03:50 hrs .

Job Summary

Pumped 100bbl drillwater from cement unit . Mixed and pump 3 bbls 1.90 sg slurry prior to releasing bottom dart telltale indicated surface release of dart . Pumped a further
86 bbl of 1.90 sg slurry no indication that bottom plug had released . Released top dart telltale indicated surface release of dart . Pumped 27 bbls drillwater at 4 bblmin
observed top plug launch . Switched to rig pumps for displacement . Flushed cement head for 2 minutes while displacing pumping at 250gpm . Increased pumps to 600 gpm .
Observed bottom plug shear at 280 psi 19 bbl early . Continued displacing at 8.5 bblmin . Slowed pumps to 4 bblmin 30 bbl prior to theoretical bump strokes . Observed
bottom plug bump 23.3bbl early ( assuming 97Yo pump efficiency ) . Bumped plug with 500 psi over initial bump pressure . Pressure tested casing to 3500 psi pumped 5 bbl .

Bled back 8 bbl ( 3 bbl line volume ) . Floats held . Good returns observed by ROV throughout the cement job . Estimate TOC 268m above casing shoe from pressure
differential observed . CIP at 03:50 hrs .

REMARKS

Drilling stopped at 2763 mMDRT after an increase in pump pressure was observed ( 4454 psi from
2800 psi ) . Only partial circulation was obtainable . The assembly was pulled to the shoe and
circulation attempted with no returns to surface . A PBL ball was dropped to isolate the lower bottom
hole assembly . Circulation was achieved at 450 gpm indicating that the drill string was blocked below
the PBL sub . Pulled out of hole to inspect the bottom hole assembly .

No accidents or incidents .

-----Page 117-----

Well Summary

1.2 Introduction

Baker Hughes INTEQ Mudlogging provided formation evaluation drill monitoring and pressure
evaluation services for Laminaria Pilot South1 from spud until Total Depth of 3338 mMDRT . Data
was processed and stored using ADVANTAGE V.1.4RO software .

Laminaria Pilot South1 was designed as a vertical appraisal well . Its objective was to acquire
sufficient data of good quality over the target reservoir intervals to attempt to establish the economic
Viability of sidetracking from the Laminaria6 to the Laminaria Pilot South1 location .

The well was spudded at 03:15 hours on the 24 May 2005 . The seabed was tagged at 374.5
MMDRT and drilling of the 914 mm ( 36 ) commenced to 410 MMDRT . The 762 mm ( 30 ) conductor
casing was seated at 407.3 mMDRT . The 311 mm ( 12 74 ) hole section was drilled riserless to 2694
MMDRT . The 244 mm ( 9 58 ) casing was run and cemented at 2688.8 mMDRT and the subsea
equipment and riser were installed .

The 216 mm ( 8 72 ) hole section was completed in two bit runs . After drilling out the 244 mm ( 9 58 )
casing a Formation Integrity Test was conducted to 1.35 sg EMW . The mud used was an AquaDrill
system weighted at 1.10 sg . Drilling of this section was delayed after a fishing trip had to be
undertaken to retrieve a nut from a dog collar that had fallen down the hole . After drilling started
the string was pulled to change the mud motor . The internal components of the motor had failed
thereby plugging the bit jets . The second bit was then run in and after a caustic pili was pumped to
correct suspected bit balling at 3003 mMDRT drilled to the well TD of 3338 mMDRT without
problems . TD was reached at 09:45 hrs on 5 June 2005 . There was no wireline logging
programme for this well . Laminaria Pilot South1 was subsequently plugged and abandoned .

Woodside Energy Ltd : Laminaria Pilot South1 1.21

Drilling Summary

Laminaria Pilot Hole South 1 was spudded at
03:15 hrs on 24 . May 2005 . The section was
drilled using seawater with guar gum sweeps
midstand and gel sweeps at each connection .
The 914 mm ( 36 ) hole section was drilled to
410m where the drill string was pulled in
preparation to run the 762 mm ( 30 ) conductor
casing .

No data for the top hole section was collected due
to an equipment malfunction at the start of drilling .

Drilling Summary

NB2 was made up to a mud motor and run in the
hole . Cement was tagged at 407m and drilled
out . Drilling of new formation commenced from
410m . The hole was drilled using seawater with
a 75 bbl guar gum sweep mid stand and a 50 bbl
gel sweep at each connection . At 2081m drilling
was delayed in order to change a pump liner .
From 1973m an additional 50 bbl guar gum
sweep was pumped at the first single of each
stand in order to improve hole cleaning . Drilling
continued to 2395m where the hole was reamed
in order to free the float valve which had become
stuck open . Subsequently 5 stands were pulled
back and a second float valve was added to the
drill string . The string was run back in the hole
and drilling continued without further incident to
the section TD of 2694m . The string was pulled
and the BHA racked back prior to running the 244
mm ( 9 58 ) casing and subsea stack .

Drilling Summary

After completion of the casing run and installation
of the riser and BOP stack . A 216 mm ( 872 )
directional drilling assembly was picked up . While
the BHA was being made a washer from a dog
collar accidentally dropped into the wellbore . A
magnet assembly was then made up and ran in
the hole to retrieve the fish . The initial attempt
was unsuccessful and reverse circulating junk
basket was run in thereafter . The fish was
successfully retrieved on the second fishing
attempt . NB3 was then run in tagging the top of
the cement at 2662m . The cement and shoe track
were drilled while displacing the hole to 1.10 sg
Aquadrill mud . 3m of new formation was then
drilled to 2697 m where an FIT was conducted to
1.35 sg EMW . Drilling of the 211 mm ( 872 ) hole
section commenced after completion of the FIT
and at 2763 m the drill string was found to be
plugged . After attempts to clear the blockage were
unsuccessful the bit was pulled out of hole to
determine the cause . At the surface the plugging
was found to be due to failure in the internal mud
motor components .

Drilling Summary

After changing out the mud motor which was
found to be the source of the plugging on the
previous bit run NB4 was attached to the same
BHA as NB3 and run in the hole . Drilling
continued to 3003m where drilling slowed to less
than 1 mhr . Suspecting a balledup bit a caustic
pill was pumped down the hole . This appeared to
clean the bit successfully and drilling re
commenced with a better ROP of about 10 mhr .
Drilling continued to the well TD of 3338m without
further incident . Bottomsup was circulated prior
to racking back the last stand of drill pipe . The
hole was then reamed before a flow check ( static )
was conducted . The drillstring was then pulled
out of the hole . An abandonment program
commenced thereafter .

Pressure Evaluation

-----Page 139-----

SECTION 4

PRESSURE EVALUATION

-----Page 140-----

41 Pressure Evaluation

4.1 Pore Pressure Evaluation

Baker Hughes INTEQ formation pressure evaluation services commenced from spud at 374.5 mMDRT .
Formation evaluation was carried out using surface sensor data collected while drilling and realtime LWD data
as well as offset data provided by the client for correlation purposes . All depths in this discussion refer to
metres Measured Depth below Rotary Table ( mMDRT ) unless otherwise stated .

Pore pressure was estimated using the method of correlating normalized Dxc trend lines with Dxc values .
This method of calculating pore pressure can only be used quantitatively in sections of homogeneous
claystones or shale and drilling with tricone bits . Dxc trends observed at shallow depths in other lithologies
and using fixed cutter bits are less reliable due to the more pronounced effects of jetting rather than bitcutting
action a shearing rather than a crushing drilling action and other factors . As such corrected Dxc data can only
be used as qualitative measurements of pore pressure .

The corrected drilling exponent Dxc was plotted continually while drilling proceeded in an attempt to identify a
normal compaction trend and any subsequent deviations from this trend which might have indicated changes
in formation pore pressure . Background gas including both liberated while drilling and while circulating off
bottom the nature of cuttings and cavings general borehole condition together with lagged mud temperatures
were the main tools used in estimating the degree of mud overbalance during drilling . At Laminaria Pilot
South1 a formation fluid density of 1.04 sg was assumed for all pressure gradient calculations .

914 mm ( 36 ) 4 311 mm ( 1274 ) Hole Sections : 374.5 m 410 m 410 m 2694 m

These hole sections were drilled with seawater and returns were dumped to seabed . While drilling riserless no
lithological data could be collected . Drilling exponent ( Dxc ) showed a normal generally rightwardsloping trend
with depth indicating normal pore pressure throughout both sections . With no lithological control and based on
the relative ease of drilling the formations with no hole stability problems encountered during drilling or the
subsequent surface casing run it was estimated that the pore pressure remained normal at 1.04 sg EMW
throughout these intervals .

216 mm ( 872 ) Hole Section : 2694 m 3338 m

A general rightwardtrending compaction line on the Dxc plot was evident from the casing shoe down to 2950
m where a leftward shift in the DxC trend can be seen indicating a possible increase in pore pressure . This
shift is also reflected in the realtime MWD resistivity plot . However due to the high overbalance maintained
while drilling it is very difficult to quantify the increase in pore pressure . Background gas levels were very low
during drilling down to 2850 m after which they started to rise as drilling approached the target formation . No
connection gas nor significant trip gas was recorded throughout the section indicating that the pore pressure
was below the mudweight of 1.10 sg . Likewise hole condition was generally good and no pressure cavings
were seen .

In the absence of conclusive overpressure parameters it can be said that the pore pressure followed the
predicted pressure profile gathered from offset wells in the Laminaria structure . The pore pressure was
predicted to be normal at 1.04 sg from the 244 mm ( 958 ) casing shoe down to 2824 m gradually increasing
to a maximum of 1.08 sg EMW at 2954 m and then back to normal at 1.04 sg EMW at 3197 m .

Woodside Energy : Laminaria Pilot South1 41414

-----Page 141-----

4.2 Pressure Evaluation

4.2 Fracture Pressure Evaluation

Fracture pressure estimation for Laminaria Pilot South1 was made using the Baker Hughes INTEQ zero
tensile strength method . For a full explanation of this method refer to INTEQ Manual MS156 The Theory and
Evaluation of Formation Pressures .

With no returns to surface it was not possible to estimate the fracture pressure through the 311 mm ( 1274 ) hole
section . The ROV observed cuttings returns at seabed while drilling throughout this section . A Formation
Integrity Test ( FIT ) was conducted at the 244mm ( 9 58 ) casing shoe with the results shown below :

Casing Test Fracture Test
Depth Casing Size Hole Size Mud Density Gradient type
EMW
mMDRT mm in mm in ( s9 ) ( s9 )
2688.8 244 9 58 216 8 2 1.10 1.5 FIT

An AquaDrill mud system weighted to 1.10 sg was used while drilling the 216 mm ( 8 12 ) section with the
ECD ranging from 1.19 sg to 1.20 sg . No mud losses were seen throughout the 216 mm hole section .

Woodside Energy Ltd : Laminaria Pilot South1 4.24

-----Page 204-----

Woodside Energy Ltd Laminaria Pilot South 1

Customer : Woodside Energy Ltd

Well : Laminaria Pilot South 1

Job Objectives :

Performance vertical well with a very long riserless 12 14 section . Verticality not an issue in comparison to performance .

Summary of Results :
Job went well one motor failure believed to be due to the drilling parameters followed in drilling out the shoe .

1.15 ? bend believed to be a little aggressive for minor correction runs but careful monitoring of the sllides involved meant that doglegs
were kept to a minimum whilst achieving a correction in the shortest distance ( time ) possible .

Discussion :

BHA Summary :

12 14
The BHA for this section performed well . Slickbore motor and bit proved invaluable in achieving this long section in one run . This BHA
did build angle in the last few hundred meters of this section .

812
This BHA coped well in the hard formation as well as being able to take advantage of the faster formations a 1.15 ? bend was in the motor .
A very steerable assembly though in rotary mode seemed to walk right though this is assumed to be due to the formation tendency .

BHA Bit Motor Hole Size MD in MD Out TVD in TVD Out Inc In Inc Out Aziln Azi Out Drig Circ

1 1 8.500 2694 2763 2693 2762 1.7 0.9 5 KE 7T 4
1 1 8.500 2763 3129 2762 3128 0.9 1.9 1 257 25 0

Table 1 BHA Summary

Motor Run Summary :

9 58 motor

A very strong motor survived well considering the punishment that it endured with such a long section in the form of vibrations high
WOB high RPM . Finished the section well seemed to still be very strong even after drilling over 2000m in ground with hard chert
stringers .

6 34 motor
The first motor used for this section chunked after only a few hours in the ground . This is believed to be due to the parameters that were

used to drill out the casing shoe . When it came time to do a correction run shortly after drilling out the shoe it was found that the motor
could not handle any weight on bit believed to be due to the chunked motor as well as having a very aggressive bit in the ground .

The second motor was exactly the same and with a more conservative approach to the drilling parameters this motor performed very well .
Higher than expected ROPs were achieved in comparison to the offset wells .

Slickbore 12 14

SDBS 8 12

Performed better then expected bit balling a slight issue believed to be due to the fact that it is a 7 bladed 5 nozzled bit . etter than
other similar sections of offset wells . Very steerable bit .

HALLIBURTON Sperry Drilling Services

Operational Overview

Sperry Dilling Services ( Halliburton ) were contracted by Woodside Energy Ltd to provide
LWDMWD services for the drilling of the well Laminaria Pilot South1 on the semisubmersible
drilling rig Atwood Eagle .

124 Hole Section :

This section was drilled utilising Sperry Drilling Services P4M system comprising Dual Gamma Ray
( DGR ) for logging purposes and a Directional Module ( DM ) for deviation control . A Dynamic
Drillstring Sensor ( DDS ) was utilsed for downhole vibration assessment . Extreme vibration was
observed in the upper less consolidated formations resulting in poor detection . Surveys and Gamma
Ray data which were missed real time were obtained from recorded data . This section was
drilled to TD at 2694.0 mMDRT in one bitrun .

872 Hole Section :

This section was drilled utilising Sperry Drilling Services P4M Triple Combo tool suite comprising
FourPhase Electromagnetic Wave Resistivity ( EWRP4 ) Dual Gamma Ray ( DGR ) Compensated
Neutron Porosity ( CNP ) and Stabilised LithoDensity ( SLD ) for logging purposes and a Directional
Module ( DM ) for deviation control . A Dynamic Drillstring Sensor ( DDS ) was utilised for downhole
vibration assessment . The first run was drilled to 2763.0 mMDRT when the bit became blocked
resulting in a trip to change out both bit and motor . The second run drilled to well TD at 3338.0 mMDRT .

2 ) . AVICV is calculated at the MWD collar using the Power Law for water based muds and the Binghams Plastic Law for oil based
muds .

3 ) . Curve mnemonics used are :

SGRC Smoothed Dual Gamma Ray Combined api

SEXP Smoothed Extra Shallow PhaseShift Derived Resistivity ohmm
SESP Smoothed Shallow PhaseShift Derived Resistivity ohmm
SEMP Smoothed Medium PhaseShift Derived Resistivity ohmm

SROP Smoothed Rate of Penetration mhr

SBD2 Smoothed Best Bin Bulk Density Compensated gcc

SCO2 Smoothed Best Bin Delta Rho gcc

SNP2 Smoothed Best Bin Near PE be

NUCL Smoothed Neutron Porosity corrected for Salinity Temperature and Pressure viv
SHSI Smoothed Hole Size Indicator in

4 ) . CNP data processed using the CNPE algorithim using the following parameters and is based on a Limestone
Matrix :

MW 3 1.10 1.105 SG

5 ) . CNP data has been reprocessed using data from the SLD hole size indicator for borehole diameter .
6 . ) Gap in Gamma Ray data from 587.5 to 592.7 mMDRT caused by slip sensor problem .

ABSTRACT

Between 15 and 27 May 2005 Fugro Survey Pty Ltd ( Fugro ) provided equipment and
personnel for the semisubmersible Mobile Offshore Drilling Unit Atwood Eagle rig move from
Laminaria5 to Laminaria South ( pilot hole ) location in Permit ACL5 in the Timor Sea Australia .

Surface positioning was provided by Fugros Multiple Reference Differential Global Positioning
System ( MRDGP3 ) and Starfix Seis Navigation Software .

The final position for the drill stem derived from DGPS observations at Laminaria South
location is :

Location Name : Laminaria South

Easting ( m ) : 174702.20
Northing ( m ) : 8822665.80

Latitude : 10238 11.01S
Longitude : 126 ? 01 37.62 E

Rig Heading : 91.18 ? ( True )

This position is 4.2m on a bearing of 220.7 ( Grid ) from the proposed Laminaria South location .

All coordinates in this report are referenced to the Geocentric Datum of Australia 1994 ( GDA94 )
and projected onto the Map Grid of Australia 1994 ( MGA94 ) Zone 52 ( CM 129 EF ) unless
otherwise stated .

All times in this report are quoted in Australian Central Standard Time ( CST ) unless otherwise
stated .

P0252 Final Report Rev 0 Pagei

-----Page 353-----

1.0

11

1.2

INTRODUCTION

Fugro Survey Pty Ltd ( Fugro ) was contracted by Woodside Energy Ltd ( Woodside ) to
provide navigation and positioning survey services on board the semisubmersible
Mobile Offshore Drilling Unit ( MODU ) Atwood Eagle during the rig move to Laminaria
South location in Permit ACL5 in the Timor Sea Australia .

A general location diagram is shown as Figure 11 .

This report details the equipment used survey parameters adopted procedures
employed and the results achieved . A section on safety is included in Section 3.0 of
this report .

Scope of Work

Personnel and equipment were provided on a 24 hour per day basis for :

5 Calibration and function testing of the survey equipment on board the rig and the
two Anchor Handling Vessels ( AHVs ) .

5 Surface navigation for the Atwood Eagle using Fugros MRDGPS ( Multi
Reference DGPS ) and Starfix Spot DGPS services .

5 Surface navigation for AHVs during anchoring operations using Starfix Spot
DGPS .

5 Final rig surface positioning for the Laminaria South location using DGPS
observations .

5 Final reporting of the positioning results .
Sequence of Events

On 15 May 2005 R. Risah and S. Bradley departed Perth for the Atwood Eagle . After
equipment calibrations the anchors were recovered at Laminaria5 at 06:00 on
23 May 2005 . The rig tow to Laminaria South commenced . The rig was positioned on
location at Laminaria South at 23:40 on 23 May 2005 . Fugro personnel departed the
rig on 26 May 2005 and returned to Perth the following day .

Further details of Fugros involvement in the rig move are presented in the Daily
Operations Reports included in Appendix A .

2.2

RESULTS
Final Position

The final position of the Atwood Eagle drill stem was established by calculating the
mean position from four hours of DGPS data logged between 05:00 and 09:00 on
24 May 2005 . During this period calculated drill stem coordinates from the primary
and secondary positioning systems were logged at a five second interval in Starfix
Seis . Data from the primary positioning system were used for the final position
calculation .

Differential GPS corrections were derived using a multireference solution with base
station data from Darwin Broome Karratha and Bali .

GDA94 geographical positions for the Laminaria South location are shown in
Table 21 .

GDA94

A copy of the original rig position field report is contained in Appendix B .

Rig Heading

The heading of the Atwood Eagle was established by calculating the average heading
during four hours of corrected gyro compass readings logged between 05:00 and

09:00 on 24 May 2005 . During this period gyro readings were logged at a five second
interval in Starfix Seis .

3.0 SAFETY
All work undertaken by Fugro personnel during the project was performed within the
guidelines of Fugros Safety Policy as defined in Fugros Safety Manual ( SMSP01 )
and Offshore Survey Safety Practices ( SMSSP26 ) .

Fugro personnel worked within all project safety guidelines and plans adopted by
Woodside and Atwood Oceanics .

No safety incidents involving Fugro personnel were reported during the project .

Fugro personnel attended a vessel induction prerig move meeting and muster drill
whilst on board .

A Project Specific Safety Plan was developed for positioning services on board the
Atwood Eagle for the Laminaria South rig move .

P0252 Final Report Rev 0 Page 31

-----Page 358-----

4.0

41

4.2

4.3

SURVEY OPERATIONS
Mobilisation

The survey team departed Perth on 15 May 2005 and arrived on board the rig on
16 May 2005 whilst it was located at Laminaria5 . Following a rig induction routine
system and function tests for the survey equipment on board the rig were completed .

General Survey Procedures

The rig was relocated from Laminaria5 Wellhead location to the proposed location of
Laminaria South with the Maersk Helper and Far Saltire connected to the tow bridle
and anchor # 6 chain respectively .

The Maersk Helper manoeuvred the rig on the anchor # 6 line an imaginary line
between anchor # 6 drop point position and proposed well location . The Far Saltire
was positioned on the anchor # 6 drop location . After anchor # 6 had been deployed
by the Far Saltire the anchor # 6 chain and wire were paidout and Maersk Helper
continued towing and positioned the rig over the proposed Laminaria South location .

After establishing that anchor # 6 was holding and the rig was maintaining its position
at Laminaria South the Far Saltire then ran anchors # 2 # 7 # 3 # 5 and # 4 . The
Maersk Helper subsequently ran anchors # 8 and # 1 .

Once all anchors were laid and the rig positioned within the specified tolerance of the
proposed Laminaria South location a systematic pretension test was conducted on all
anchors .

During the deployment of each anchor the AHVs were provided with a waypoint and
the corresponding runline via the Wombat telemetry system . The AHVs ran out the
anchor chain along this line to the desired drop point . The anchor chain was stretched
out and the anchor lowered to the seabed . After confirming that the anchor was
holding the vessel then stripped the chain chaser back to the rig .

The Atwood Eagle was positioned over the Laminaria South location with all anchoring
and pretensioning operations complete at 23:40 on 23 May 2005 . Final position data
were logged between 05:00 and 09:00 on 24 May 2005 . A rig positioning field report
was issued to the Woodside Survey QC representative and the Woodside Company
Representative ( see Appendix B ) .

Demobilisation

The remote navigation systems onboard the AHVs were switched off on 24 May 2005
upon completion of all rig move operations . The navigation equipment onboard the rig
remained online and operational to monitor the rigs position during drilling operations
at Laminaria South .

Fugro personnel departed the rig on 26 May 2005 and returned to Perth the following
day .

P0252 Final Report Rev 0 Page 41

-----Page 359-----

5.2

EQUIPMENT CALIBRATION
DGPS Navigation Integrity Check

In order to check the correct operation of the navigation systems installed on board the
Atwood Eagle DGPS data were logged for 30 minutes on 17 May 2005 whilst the rig
was located at Laminaria5 .

A comparison of the primary and secondary DGPS was also conducted . The results
from both of these tests are provided in Table 51 .

GDA94 MGA CM 129 ? E
Easting ( m ) Northing ( m )

Established Well Coordinates 174923.90 8823909.03

Observed Coordinates 174926.95 8823908.98

Difference 3.05 0.05
Primary Navigation 174926.95 8823908.98
Secondary Navigation 174924.34 8823909.79
Difference 12.61 0.81

TABLE 51 : DGPS NAVIGATION INTEGRITY CHECK

The DGPS check described above demonstrated that the navigation systems on board
the Atwood Eagle were set up and working correctly .

A positioning check list was completed at Laminaria South location to confirm the
proposed rig position and to ensure that the correct geodetic datum transformation
and projection parameters were being used . Geodetic calculations were performed
using both Starfix Seis and the offIline geodetic calculation package GEO .

Details of all positioning checks are provided in Appendix C .
Gyro Compass Calibration

The calibration of the survey gyro compass was carried out on 16 May 2004 whilst the
rig was located at Laminaria5 .

A series of observations were made to the sun from which the rig heading was
calculated . The calculated values were then compared to the observed gyro compass
values logged in Starfix Seis and a mean CO value of 490.30 was determined . This
correction was applied in the navigation suite .

Details of the gyro calibration are included in Appendix C .

P0252 Final Report Rev 0 Page 51

6.0 SURVEY PARAMETERS

6.1 Geodetic Parameters

All coordinates are referenced to the Geocentric Datum of Australia 1994 ( GDA94 )
unless otherwise noted . The Global Positioning System ( GPS ) operates on the World
Geodetic System 1984 ( WGS84 ) datum . Fugros Differential GPS Reference Stations
are currently defined in the International Terrestrial Reference Frame 2000 ( ITRF2000
Epoch 2005.25 ) datum . Due to the continual refinement of the WGS84 reference
frame for all cases the transformation parameters indicate that the WGS84 and

ITRF2000 reference frames are essentially identical .

Datum World Geodetic System 1984 ( WGS84 )
Reference Spheroid : World Geodetic System 1984

Semi Major Axis : 6378137.000m

Inverse flattening : 298.257223563

Datum Geocentric Datum of Australia 1994 ( GDA94 )
Reference Spheroid : Geodetic Reference System 1980 ( GRS80 )
Semi Major Axis : 6378137.000m

Inverse flattening : 298.257222101

The following seven parameter datum transformation ( Table 61 ) was used in Fugros
software to transform WGS84 ( ITRF2000 Epoch 2005.50 ) coordinates to GDA94
coordinates . These parameters are calculated from the 14 parameter transformation
defined by Geoscience Australia . Fugro follows the Coordinate Frame Rotation

convention ( as defined by UKOOA ) for datum transformations .

Transformation Parameters from WGS84 ( ITRF2000 Epoch 2005.50 ) to GDA94

0.0156m

# 0.01445

0.0348m

# 0.013050

0.0513m

# 0.015037

TABLE 61 : TRANSFORMATION PARAMETERS

Map Grid of Australia .

5 May 2005 Atwood Eagle Rig Move Procedures Laminaria 5 to Laminaria South ( Pilot Hole ) Revision 2

LI

2.0
21

INTRODUCTION
General

For the purpose of this document Woodside Energy Limited shall be referred to as WEL
and Atwood Oceanics Australia shall be referred to as Atwood .

A requirement exists to move the semisubmersible drilling unit Atwood Eagle from her
present position at Laminaria 5 to the proposed location at Laminaria South ( Pilot Hole )

When the last anchor PCC is racked at present position all rig and vessel consumables
will be recorded in the rig move log at this time .

The distance from Laminaria 5 to Laminaria South is approximately 0.7nm

The proposed Laminaria South location is as follows :

Latitude : 10 ? 38 10.904 South
Longitude : 126 ? OD 37.710 East
Easting 174 705.00mE
Northing 8 822 669.00 m N
Water depth : 353 metres or 1158 feet .
Rig heading : 090 ? ( T )

The estimated period of time required for each stage of the rig move ( without delays and not
allowing for run in time ) is as follows :

Mooring recovery and departure from Laminaria 5 30 hours
Passage to Laminaria South 1 hour

Anchor deployment and ballasting 30 hours
Anchor pretensioning and final positioning 06 hours
Total Time 67 hours

e. Rig will be at transit draft .
e Two AHVs will be available for anchor recovery at Laminaria 5
e Two AHVs will be available for anchor deployment at Laminaria South

The two AHVs assigned to the Eagle are the Maersk Helper and the Far Saltire .

PREAMBLE

General

The purpose of this document is to ensure that the Atwood Eagle rig move operation from
Laminaria 5 location to the proposed Laminaria South location is conducted in a safe and
efficient manner .

All key personnel shall be fully briefed by the WEL Marine Representative prior to the
commencement of operations to ensure a full understanding of these procedures . This
meeting will be documented .

These approved procedures shall be followed as closely as circumstances permit having due

Page 4 of 16

-----Page 397-----

5 May 2005 Atwood Eagle Rig Move Procedures Laminaria 5 to Laminaria South ( Pilot Hole ) Revision 2

regard for the limitations of the unit and its assisting vessels . Should any deviation from these
procedures be deemed necessary the WEL Well Site Manager shall be advised immediately .
Due consideration must be given to any and all effects of such a deviation .

All rig move vessels will be issued with a copy of this rig move procedure prior to the
commencement of the operation . The vessel Masters will be fully briefed and are required to
review the procedure and comment accordingly .

The anchor tensions during recovery at Laminaria 5 should be maintained at all times to
ensure that the chain or wire does not contact the sub sea infrastructure . A minimum tension
table is contained in this document and shall be referred to and tensions monitored and
maintained on each winch to ensure touch down points are clear of the sub sea infrastructure .

A prerig move meeting will be held onboard prior to the commencement of operations where
all key personnel as described in Section 3 shall be fully briefed to ensure a full
understanding of these procedures .

Prior to the commencement of anchor deployment operations weather forecasts shall be
obtained and a suitable weather window identified to allow each stage of the operation to
be safely completed without interruption .

4.0 SUPPORT
41 Vessels

At least two Anchor Handling Vessels ( AHVs ) will be provided for the tow and anchor
deployment at the proposed location

The tow from Laminaria 5 to the proposed Laminaria South location will be
conducted by one AHV with the other remaining connected to the # 6 anchor .

Towing AHV will have a minimum Bollard Pull of 175 tonnes . ( MOM 21.3.2 )
All AHVs will be equipped with the following gear in full working order

e JoystickPoscon control .

e. Main tow wire plus a spare tow wire .

e. Double anchor handling drum ( desirable ) .

e. Chain Gypsies suitable for 3 14 chain .

e Hydraulic towing pins and Sharks JawsKarm Forks .

e. Open stern with movable roller for anchor decking etc

e 1x TJ Hock ( previously checked for cracks and faults ) .

e 1x CGrapnel ( previously checked for cracks and faults ) .

e 2x Deepwater Enclosed Swivels .

e. Adequate 76mm chaser wires ( minimum diameter ) .

All vessels must be suitably manned in accordance with MSN 1682 ( M ) and be capable of
24 hours continuous operation in all respects . If any vessel can not provide 24 hour
coverage WEL is to be advised immediately .

The WEL Marine Representative is to ascertain the vessel manning prior to departure .

4.2 Navigation Package

A DGPS fully redundant navigation package will be provided for anchor recovery operations
at Laminaria 5 location and for anchor deployment operations at the proposed Laminaria
South locations .

The rig move package will be capable of monitoring the rigs position during all stages of the
rig move operation together with the positions of the AHVs during anchor deployment .

Both AHVs will be equipped with a navigation and gyro system linked by telemetry to the
rig system to ensure the correct deployment of anchors .

The installation and operation of the navigation package shall be the responsibility of the Rig
Positioning Supervisor who will provide continuous position information to all interested
parties as required .

The navigation system shall be calibrated and operated in accordance with the survey
contractors procedures and also WEL requirements as directed by the WEL Marine
Representative .

Rig positioning equipment should be onboard and operational at least 24 hours prior to
commencement of anchor recovery operations at the present location to allow adequate time
for installation set up calibration and system checks .

5.0 ANCHOR RETRIEVAL AT LAMINARIA 5
5.1 GENERAL

After the well program has been suspended and the rig has been disconnected from
the sea floor the rig will deballast and prepare to pull anchors .

WEL will then make a decision to proceed with the anchor handling .
The rig will be moved to the south of location and clear of all subsea infrastructure .
The anchors 4 5 and 7 will be recovered first .

The rig will then be moved to the north of location and clear of all subsea
infrastructure .

Maersk Helper will be secured to the tow bridle .

If necessary the # 7 anchor will be lowered below the hull to prevent interference
during the recovery of # 8 .

Anchors 1 3 8 and 2 will be recovered in that order .
Rig will be moved south of location by shortening up on # 6 anchor wire .

Far Saltire will unseat the # 6 anchor and the rig will make the crossover to chain and
continue heaving until 2000 feet of chain is out .

Far Saltire will manoeuvre towards the # 6 drop point whilst the Maersk Helper
manoeuvres towards the 62 run line .

Due regard shall be taken of the practice of good seamanship throughout .

Contingency :

In the event that only one AHV is available at the commencement of anchor retrieval
operations the following retrieval sequence will apply .

Rig will be moved south of location to Position 2 .
AHV will retrieve # 4 and # 5 anchors .
Rig will be moved north of location to Position 1 .

AHV will retrieve # 1 and # 8 anchors .

Page 10 of 16

-----Page 403-----

5 May 2005 Atwood Eagle Rig Move Procedures Laminaria 5 to Laminaria South ( Pilot Hole ) Revision 2

The second AHV must be available at this point for anchor retrieval operation to continue .

Pass the # 3 PCC to Far Saltire and chase to anchor .

Maersk Helper connects to tow bridle .

Retrieve # 3 anchor .

Far Saltire retrieves # 2 anchor .

Maersk Helper maintains tension on the tow bridle and the rig is moved south of location
and clear of infrastructure by heaving on # 6 and # 7 anchor wires .

Far Saltire retrieves # 7 anchor .

Far Saltire will unseat the # 6 anchor and the rig will make the crossover to chain and
continue heaving until 2000 feet of chain is out .

8.2

ANCHOR DEPLOYMENT AT LAMINARIA SOUTH ( Pilot Hole )

General
The Atwood Eagle is to moor at the proposed location with a deviated 8 anchor spread on a
heading of 0902 ( T ) .

The MODU is fitted with :
8 x 12 tonne Stevpris Mk . V anchors ( Fluke angles set at 41 ? )
8 ea 314 in x 3200 ft continuous chain
8 ea 312in x 10000 ft mooring Wire Rope
8 ea Baldt Connecting Links
8 ea Ball Swivels on mooring wire
8 ea Deepwater Enclosed Swivels
A permanent chain chasing system is installed consisting of ( PCC ) :
8 ea Permanent Chain Chasers ( PC ) w 3 .25in 30 link chains
8ea317in x 120 ft PC Pendant Wires ( PCC )

Anchor Deployment General Discussion

Anchor deployment operations at the proposed Laminaria South location will be carried out
with two AHVs The Maersk Helper and the Far Saltire .

The special requirements for deploying a Stevpris type anchor will be adhered to . The AHVs
Master will ensure that the anchor orientation is correct during anchor deployment . If the
anchor orientation is incorrect then this must be corrected prior to proceeding with anchor
deployment .

Note : 2 anchors and associated jewellery will be inspected as a matter of policy during
each rig move . Before deployment at Laminaria South # 7 and # 1 anchors will be decked and
inspected .

Conventional Anchor Handling Procedures

This procedure covers the conventional handling of Stevpris anchors .

1 ) 85Maersk Helper will be connected to the main tow bridle . Far Saltire will remain
connected to the # 6 anchor

2 ) The MODU will be manoeuvred to the Laminaria South location .
3 ) The AHV will pay out 100m ( 3004 ft ) and take tension on the chain .
4 ) The rig will drive out chain as necessary .

5 ) The AHV must maintain tension on the work wire to ensure the anchor orientation
remains the same .

6 ) Rig will pay out about 300 ft of chain and stop to change the winch to dynamic mode .

7 ) Chain pay out speed and AHV bollard pull is monitored so the chain is kept off the
bolster .

8 ) Rig continues to pay out chain to 3200 ft while the AHV increases bollard pull and
horizontal distance away from the rig .

9 ) When the 3200ft of chain is out the rig makes the crossover to wire . The AHV will
decrease its bollard pull to reduce the tensions at the fairlead but maintain adequate
distance from the rig while the crossover is made . During this process chain will be

Page 13 of 16

-----Page 406-----

5 May 2005 Atwood Eagle Rig Move Procedures Laminaria 5 to Laminaria South ( Pilot Hole ) Revision 2

allowed to rest on the bolster . The crossover is estimated to take 2040 minutes . If
required the AHV may retension the work wire at this time .

10 ) Once the crossover has been made the rig pays out wire to required amount while the
AHV moves to the anchor location .
11 ) When the rig has completed paying out 900 feet of wire the AHV will continue
to payout work wire to 1.2 times the water depth .

12 ) The AHV will lower the anchor when instructed by Atwood Eagle Control by paying
out work wire and slowly reducing power until the anchor is on the seabed .

13 ) Once the anchor is on the seafloor Survey takes a fix of the vessel .

14 ) The anchor will be given time to soak into the seabed and the rig will tension the
mooring line to ensure the anchor is holding .

15 ) Sufficient tension must be maintained on the anchor wires ( 300 kips ) to enable the AHV
to chase back to the rig

16 ) The AHV then chases back to the rig and passes the PCC wires back to the rig .

17 ) The tension on the mooring lines is brought to the operating tension of 335 kips for this
water depth and the anchor position calculated by the amount of line out .

18 ) Design rig heading is 090 ? T

Anchor ReOrientation

The following procedure will apply in the event that an anchor is incorrectly oriented prior to
running .

1 ) Rig heavesin on chain to 200 .

2 ) AHV heavesin on work wire to 150 over the stern roller .

3 ) AHV reduces power and allows anchor and chain to slip through the collar .
4 ) AHV increases power and chases back out to the anchor .

5 ) AHV maintains power as rig heaves in on chain .

6 ) Operations may continue when the rig has verified the correct orientation .

8.3

Approach to location for commencement of anchor deployment shall not be made until :

1 ) Permission to do so has been obtained from the OIM and the WEL Drilling
Representative .

2 ) Weather forecasts have been obtained and a weather window has been identified of
sufficient duration to allow for uninterrupted anchor deployment

The following anchor deployment sequence assumes :
10 ) One AHSV will be towing on the rigs tow bridle .

2 ) That one AHSV will be on the tow bridle and one will be attached to the # 6 anchor
for deployment .

Positioning of the rig Anchor Deployment Specific Discussion

1 ) Rig will be manoeuvred from the Laminaria 5 location with the Maersk Helper secured to
the main tow bridle and the Far Saltire secured to the # 6 anchor . Approximately 2000 feet
of chain will be deployed on the # 6 anchor for this manoeuvre .

2 ) The # 6 anchor attached to Far Saltire will be deployed and set on bottom .

3 ) Prior to the crossover being made on # 6 Maersk Helper will increase power and the rig
position monitored to ensure the anchor is holding .

4 ) The Far Saltire will bring the # 6 PCC back to the rig .
5 ) The Maersk Helper will then move the rig to the location .

6 ) The # 2 PCC will be passed to the Far Saltire . The # 2 anchor will be deployed . This
anchor is designed to be positioned 240m from subsea infrastructure . Rig and vessel wire
paid out lengths must be closely monitored and compared with vessel position from the
fairlead .

7 ) Anchors 3 and 7 will be deployed next .
8 ) Maersk Helper will be released from the tow bridle .

9 ) Anchors 1 and 5 8 and 4 will be deployed next . NOTE : Anchors 8 @ 1 are in the direction
of subsea infrastructure . Rig and vessel wire paid out lengths must be closely monitored
and compared with vessel position from the fairlead .

10 ) After all anchors are tensioned to working tension the rig will then ballast down to drilling
draft .

Note :
A : At any time either boat will be able to do the others task .
B : Due concerns must be given to the weather and currents during anchor handling .

C : If the surveyors equipment fails at a critical time during the anchoring operations will be
shut down until the pic is confident of continuing with mooring operations .

D : When bolstering the anchors the anchor will be placed on the bolster in the proper position .
Not upside down .

E : Good communications will be kept with the AHSV and the rig at all times .

F : A record of all connecting links that are used is to be kept by the rig and each AHSV .

9.0

10.0

ANCHOR PRETENSIONING

When anchor deployment is completed the anchors should be pretensioned to ensure
adequate holding .

Each pair of opposite anchors ( usually commencing with the primary anchors ) is tensioned to
220 tonnes ( 485 kips ) and then slackened down to approximately 152 tones min . ( 335 kips ) .

Anchors will be pretensioned in the following opposite pairs :
No . 1 and No . 5
No . 4 and No . 8
No . 2 and No . 6
No . 3 and No . 7

During anchor pretensioning winch house tensions will be checked against motor amps and
control room readouts .

When all anchors have been successfully pretensioned the tensions will be adjusted for
working at the Laminaria 5 location .

ANCHOR SLIPPAGE

If anchor slippage occurs during pretensioning the anchor may need to be redeployed in a
different location . The following comments are to be taken into account when repositioning a
particular anchor .

Check the orientation of the anchor before redeploying .

If the anchor orientation is incorrect the AHV must reorientate it . When this is done the
anchor can be deployed in its design position .

If the anchor orientation was correct consideration should be given to running out more rig
wire and deploying the anchor beyond the design position .

If the decision is made to run the anchor off the bearing of the design position this revised
bearing should not exceed 5 ? .

The rig will need to retrieve wire and chain in order that the rerun anchor cable lies in a
straight line from the fairlead if the anchor is to be deployed off bearing .

Note : The proximity of sub sea infrastructure must be taken into account when
considering changing the bearing or length of anchors that are slipping .

REPORTING

The WEL Marine Representative will ensure that all used equipment is correctly recorded
upon deployment and all unused equipment is correctly manifested for return .

The Masters of the AHVs should keep account of all mooring equipment used and advise the
WEL Marine Representative accordingly .

The WEL Marine Representative will wherever possible correctly record the ID numbers and
positions of all equipment deployed together with the purpose of deployment

The WEL Marine Representative will also record details of any known or apparent damage to
additional mooring equipment rig equipment or rig moving vessels .

All results of the report shall be passed onto the WEL Drilling Representative .
